Business News

The Golden Tide at the End of the Financial Day 74

Record Breaking Discovery

Approaching the 800 Tael Mark

Soaring Up 14 Taels and 4 Mace Yesterday, February 16th, during this major closing period for standard gold, new records were continuously set, having already broken through the 790 tael mark. The upward trend intensified and progressed very well. However, the intra-day rise did not exceed two or three taels. The exchange rate changed from loose to tight, with the listed price extended by half a block, indicating unclear and hidden conditions. Apparently, foreign firms were settling accounts, and market sentiment became stronger. Demand exceeded supply. Firms such as Yongfeng, Fuchang, Yuansheng, etc., all made purchases, while Yuanmao, Yongyuan, Yuanxing, Yongji, and others mostly sold off. This was likely due to overseas silver market reports rising in the previous day's telegrams, causing the gold price to be low early in the morning. Afterwards, buyers increased constantly, and the exchange rate improved. Especially due to widespread rumors that the Chinese government plans to establish a gold standard, or that it could be implemented in Liaoning. As a result, general speculators and merchants became enthusiastic and purchased aggressively. The market situation suddenly took off, rising sharply by more than ten taels, remarkably seeing a new peak of 796 taels again. Because of the usual custom, the market will be closed due to the New Year holiday. The market will be closed for the next two days (the 17th and 18th) and will resume normal business on the 19th.

The Atmosphere for a Gold Standard Intensifies From the opening of the April market at 777 taels and 5 mace in the morning, it decreased by 3 taels and 6 mace. Because the major silver bar from the previous day had already risen by six-eighths and the silver price had increased by one-fourth, private telegrams also increased by one-eighth, followed by 77 taels. Subsequently, due to purchases from Yong, etc., it immediately rose to 81 taels and 3 mace. Afterwards, there were occasional fluctuations of one or two taels, but Yuanmao, Yongshun, Wanxing, Yuanxing, Yong, etc., sold off, resulting in a depreciation of two taels. When the price was first announced, it was around 80 taels, and the exchange rate had already increased, calculated at 125 for British gold and 125 for American gold. Japanese gold decreased by 1 fen and 7.5 li, then retreated to 79 taels, 3 to 4 mace. However, internally it was quite different. Mitsui bought June 2 pence, and also did a three-month transaction with Korea for Citibank at $28.3125. In the market, Taikang, Runhong, Lizhi, Fengyong, etc., all made purchases, so the price progressed all the way, increasing by 5 to 6 taels. Later, British gold became tighter, and banks transacted at 1 penny and 875 li, driving the price up by 5 to 6 taels, reaching 91 taels. Yuanmao, Yong, etc., sold off, falling back by more than 3 taels. At 11 AM, it was calculated at 87 taels and a half. In the afternoon, it presented another peak. Yuancheng, Yuanheng, etc., successively competed to buy, and people's minds became more enthusiastic. The buying side was very strong, but there were very few sellers. As a result, the market atmosphere was extremely lively. The wind surged until noon, reaching 96 taels. However, from 11:30 AM to 11:45 AM, there were slight fluctuations of two or three taels. As it approached the close, it went back by one tael. When the market closed, it was calculated at 95 taels and a half, soaring by 14 taels and 4 mace compared to last Saturday. The spot price was 5 mace. The maximum price change during the half-day was 19 taels, and the minimum price was 77 taels. The spot price opened at 75 taels and closed at 95 taels. The price has been changed to 856 taels and 2 mace, calculated from 75 to 76 taels to 65 to 66 taels. At noon, it was only calculated at slightly over 60 taels. Registration was at 86 taels for February, 89 taels for March, 96 taels for April, and 86 taels for supplementary water.

Transaction Volume Not Large as Usual Due to the holiday season, there were no excessively large transactions among various firms. Yongfeng, Yuansheng, Taikangrun, Fuchang, Zhifengyong, Yuanheng, Dadecheng, etc., all made purchases. Futaiheng, Changxiang, Yuantai, Shunli, Wanxing occasionally bought and sold. Yuanmao was the top seller, with approximately one thousand several hundred bars. Changshengyong and scattered households sold slightly. The Dalian gang had a total of more than 12 million, breaking even. The Guang gang had a small number of transactions.

Exchange Rate Listing Lengthened 75

Internal Trading Tight · · Many Account Settlements

Yesterday, the HSBC listed exchange rates were lengthened by half a block, due to the report of rising silver prices in British and American banks the previous day. British gold was lengthened by 125, calculated as 1 penny and 175 li for the first order. American gold was only lengthened by 125, calculated as 27 yuan and 75 cents. Indian exchange increased by 75, calculated as 77 rupees. French francs increased by 6 yuan, calculated as 710 yuan. German exchange increased by 1 yuan, calculated as 117 marks. Japanese and foreign currency increased by half a yuan, calculated as 69 guilders and 25 cents. Singapore exchange decreased by 1 tael and 7 mace and 5 li, calculated as 202 taels. Hong Kong remained the same, calculated as 78 taels and a half. However, the internal trading situation of the banks was tightening, likely because importers and British and American tobacco firms were settling accounts. Standard gold turned from weak to strong. During this major closing period, a new high price of 796 taels, which had never been reached before, actually occurred, breaking the previous record, and 800 taels is right in front of us. This is truly due to the general public's extremely high expectations regarding the rumored change to a gold standard. Demand exceeds supply, and therefore the exchange market is even more sharp. By the noon closing, British gold decreased by 125, American gold decreased by 25, and Japanese gold increased by 1 fen and a half compared to last Saturday. The external and internal trading conditions were truly different. Chinese firms such as Fuchang, etc., slightly dumped British gold, totaling about 100,000 pounds. Banks such as Mitsui and Zhejiang Industrial all absorbed. Yufengyong has already settled with Mitsui, etc., and various firms have transacted several tens of thousands of pounds with each other. Also, American gold was transacted between parties for over 100,000 yuan. Also, Fuchang, etc., sold 100,000 to 200,000 yuan to Mitsui, which is a hedging strategy. However, there was very little Japanese gold trading, because the hedging was not agreeable. Since the gold market will be closed in the afternoon, there will be no substantial trading. It is said that the major silver bars may see a decline tonight.

Confused Foreign Cents, Silver Discounts Not Opened 77

Due to the Great New Year's Eve of Customary Tradition... The silver and money industry generally announces the grand closing. Yesterday, during the grand comparison period of the abolished lunar New Year (namely, commonly known as the Great New Year's Eve), the silver and money industry's busy and complex procedures for collection, delivery, and various closing procedures were beyond comparison. Therefore, the situation was extremely chaotic. Due to customary traditions, there were constant rules that no one paid attention to, resulting in generally unlimited transactions and market prices in the market. Foreign cents rose and fell suddenly, also without any order. The early market was 7 mace, 2 fen, and 2 li, a decrease of 3 li compared to the previous day's noon market. The noon market suddenly rebounded by 1 li, calculated as 7 mace, 7 fen, and 3 li. In the bank's trading, inter-bank trading in the early market was 800,000, and the noon market was 1,200,000. Because yesterday had already announced the grand closing, discount ticket transactions were completely stopped, so the price was not opened. A Glimpse of Standard Yarn and Cotton Since the New Year 81

The Atmosphere Seems to Carry a Cotton Famine Color

Manpower is Inflated, Rising Around 30 Taels Since the New Year's Day start for standard yarn, prices have been gradually increasing. Each price has increased by about 30 taels compared to the end of last year. The initial cause of this intense price increase was the National Government's reform of the unified cotton yarn tax, driving actual sales. Various gangs bought about 70,000 to 80,000 bales, emptying out bottom stocks and strengthening manufacturers' attitudes. Coupled with the golden tide surging and the silver price falling miserably, foreign cotton could not be imported. The related yarn market was difficult to ease fundamentally, making people's minds more determined. The intentions of a certain industrialist were particularly strong, absorbing a considerable amount. The raw material prices for the shorts were soaring, presenting unstable conditions. The market situation became increasingly high. Although several factories hedged before the market closed, it was still difficult to reduce the buying trend. The day traders were the most numerous among the shorts. During the most intense price increase, the two major security deposit households dissolved over a million taels. It is difficult to predict what will happen in the future. The total turnover of manpower on both the buying and selling sides of the exchange was 212,350 bales. The net turnover by the bullish manpower was 74,950 bales. February was 21,550 bales, March was 42,550 bales, April was 50,200 bales, May was 45,250 bales, June was 40,200 bales, and July was 11,700 bales. Hankou Cotton Prices Surge 10 Taels The situation of the Hankou standard cotton futures price rising 10 taels compared to last year is rare. It is actually due to the blow of exchange rates, the miserable fall in silver prices, and the crazy rise in gold prices. The calculation of Indian cotton is extremely expensive in silver, making it difficult to import. The cotton produced in our own country is not sufficient to supply. Foreign cotton cannot be purchased, so speculators absorb a large amount, and the market rapidly rises. Before the market closes, it is very likely that there will be a cotton famine. The terror of the shorts reaches its peak. However, the world produces a lot, but exchange rates do not ease, making it difficult to come in. Therefore, the buyers' morale is firm. The Japanese firm Toyo buys about 70,000 to 80,000 piculs. The general retail investors follow suit. The most sellers are from the Hankou gang, and the losses are huge. The future of the cotton market is difficult to predict. In short, the bottom stock is thin, and the exchange market is not long, with no fundamental flaws. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency interviewed Industry Minister Kong Xiangxi at his private residence on West Adams Road yesterday afternoon. Secretary Wang received the reporter. Only a few secretaries and attendants will accompany Mr. Kong. (2) It was previously heard that industrial bonds would be issued for 15 million to handle major industries such as sugar factories, textile factories, and sulfuric acid factories, but there has been no progress recently. This is a common inquiry to Minister Kong. Secretary Wang then conveyed Mr. Kong's words, stating that the government is comprehensively planning the Sino-Russian trade issue. Since Representative Mo of the Sino-Russian negotiations returned to China and arrived in Beijing, he has repeatedly consulted with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Although this matter is related to the Ministry of Industry, it must wait for the government to determine a comprehensive plan. The issuance of industrial bonds was two years ago, and there has been no progress recently.

Report from National Goods Inspection Delegation Leader Zhou Guojun 87

Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia Greatly Need National Goods

The Shanghai National Goods Factories United Association previously organized an inspection delegation to the Southeast Asian Islands and appointed Zhou Guojun as its leader. All delegation members have now returned to China, but Mr. Zhou remains in Shantou due to other matters. Yesterday, Mr. Zhou sent a long letter to the association, reporting on the trip and his impressions. His report is highly relevant to promoting national goods. The following is a telegraphic transcription of the original text:

Respectfully, I, Zhou Guojun, was publicly appointed by your association as the leader of the Southeast Asia Inspection Delegation. Together with the delegation members, we sailed south for three months. Departing from Shanghai and passing through Hong Kong and French Indochina, we arrived in Singapore on November 20th of last year. We entered the Malay States and reached ____. On December 23rd, we went to ____, and on the 28th, we returned to ____ and then went to the Dutch East Indies, Sumatra and Java. On January 15th of this year, we first returned to Singapore and then came back to China. In addition to a detailed report to be submitted upon my return to Shanghai, I would like to briefly present my observations regarding the promotion of national products.

The Southeast Asian Islands are located in the tropics, with a warm climate and abundant resources. Due to historical and geographical relations with our country, there are approximately five million overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, who are hardworking, resilient, diligent, and frugal. They are the leaders of the Southeast Asian industry and control the economic lifeline. While foreigners are also adept at selling local products, the distribution of imported goods within the region is impossible without the participation of the overseas Chinese. The social life of the overseas Chinese is largely the same as in China. Although there are some who forget their origins, most still retain their ancestral customs and habits. Therefore, the demand for national goods is extremely high.

The patriotism and enthusiasm of the overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia for using national goods have long been recognized by the people of China. If China's industry is developed enough to meet the needs of the overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia and other ethnic groups, and if we improve our products and promote them effectively, the prospects are limitless. Last year, the price of local products plummeted, an unprecedented event. Bankruptcies were frequently reported, and unemployment increased daily. However, due to the backwardness of the colonial economy and the low standard of living, most daily necessities are imported from abroad. The goods consumed are mostly necessities rather than valuable luxury items. Therefore, even in the midst of panic and weak purchasing power, it is still impossible to stop consumption. Furthermore, the appreciation of gold and the depreciation of silver, coupled with the commendable enthusiasm of overseas Chinese for using national goods, mean that the promotion of national goods in Southeast Asia will not be greatly affected by the decline in trade and will instead present an excellent opportunity for promotion.

The main reasons for the sluggish trade between China and Southeast Asia are twofold: (1) China is still in the position of supplying raw materials to others, and (2) the content of life in overseas Chinese society is not entirely the same as in China, and domestic manufacturers have failed to adapt to their needs and provide appropriate supplies. Therefore, apart from food and agricultural products, the quality of manufactured national goods entering Southeast Asia is only barely satisfactory. Thus, miscellaneous goods account for the largest share of sales. There are countless varieties of miscellaneous goods, the most popular in the market being mountain products such as bamboo, clothing, bamboo chairs, and other utensils; raw oil, grains, incense, paper materials, seafood, tea, utensils, fresh fruits, and vegetables are also abundant. As for manufactured national goods, apart from cigarettes, towels, threads, socks, and clothing, which are occasionally sold to natives or other ethnic communities, the rest are mainly consumed by millions of overseas Chinese.

Foreigners use political means to carry out economic aggression, with the former preceding the latter. China has vast land and abundant resources, but unfortunately, we cannot extract them effectively. Our industry is backward, and we are far behind others. In order to break the deadlock, we hope that compatriots at home and abroad will revitalize industry, improve products, use our patriotic and wealthy overseas Chinese as a backing, promote Sino-Southeast Asian commerce, develop foreign trade, and work together towards this goal. Our export trade to Southeast Asia will undoubtedly increase day by day. This can be stated with certainty. I am sending this preliminary report, and I will continue to report in detail in the future.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Urges Members to Report Total Capital 88

Collection of Membership Fees to Have a Basis

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter yesterday to 67 trade associations, including the yarn industry, rice shops, shipping industry, silk factories, and clothing industry, as well as store members, stating:

In accordance with the Chamber's articles of association, membership fees should be collected based on the total capital of each member. Therefore, each member should report their total capital in advance and then pay membership fees in accordance with the regulations. The Chamber has already issued a notice setting a deadline for reporting. While many members have reported and paid their fees on time, there are also many who have failed to do so by the deadline. The Chamber's expenses are funded by membership fee income. Without the reported capital of each member, the Chamber cannot collect membership fees, which hinders the Chamber's operations. All trade associations are members of the Chamber and should fulfill their membership obligations. It is inappropriate to ignore the urging of the Chamber. Therefore, it was decided at the 31st Standing Committee meeting on the 12th of this month to extend the deadline to the end of February. All members must report their total capital and pay their membership fees by then. This letter serves as a final reminder. Please report to the Chamber on time and do not delay further. This is of utmost importance.

Anti-Opium Society Petitions Central Government to Stop Opium Public Sale 89

Public Sale Not Without Cause

Should Be Strictly Prohibited

The Chinese National Anti-Opium Society believes that rumors of opium public sale have been circulating widely recently. It has joined forces with various related organizations to strongly protest, as previously reported. The other day, the Honorary Chairman of the Society, Tang Shaochuan, convened a meeting of the Standing Committee to discuss countermeasures. It was decided to petition the Central Government and instruct the National Anti-Opium Bureau to effectively ban opium and other drugs, and to instruct local party branches to prohibit the promotion of opium public sale, in order to emphasize the prohibition of opium. The original petition is quoted below:

Petition for the strict prohibition of opium and the prevention of public sale based on the teachings of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen.

The evils of opium are endless. The late Premier's anti-opium teachings stated that opium business is absolutely incompatible with the national government authorized by the people. He also said that anyone who advocates legalizing opium business is a public enemy of the people, and any responsible government agency that abandons the fight against opium for its own private interests is an act of treason. The KMT's platform has clear provisions for the prohibition of opium. Our Society follows the teachings of the late Premier and adheres to the Party's platform to launch anti-opium movements. Fortunately, with the completion of the Northern Expedition, we promoted the government's implementation of a prohibition policy.

Recently, however, we have received rumors that the anti-opium authorities are changing the policy of complete prohibition and are now preparing to implement a national public sale system. Although the Central Anti-Opium Committee has stated that this is inaccurate, rumors are rife, with many claiming to have solid evidence. It is said that a certain foreign adviser at the Jianghai Customs is drafting regulations for the public sale of opium under the commission of a certain authority, with the sole purpose of raising funds, with an estimated annual income of 80 to 100 million yuan. The Ministry of Finance has also sent Li Jihong, who was most active in handling opium public sale in the past, to Taiwan to investigate the local opium public sale system in preparation for imitation, causing opposition from the local overseas Chinese. Liu Ruiheng, the current Chairman of the Central Anti-Opium Committee, did not explicitly deny this in an interview with the Mainichi Shimbun reporter. Moreover, Li Jihong, who went to Taiwan to investigate public sale, and Wu Liande, who openly advocated public sale, have both been formally appointed as members of the Central Anti-Opium Committee. Thus, the anti-opium authorities are already taking steps to adopt a public sale policy.

The National Government has clearly promulgated a policy of absolute prohibition of opium, which is known throughout the country and abroad. Although the policy has not been fully implemented in recent years, such as the special opium tax in Hunan and Hubei, the open sale of land in Guangdong and Guangxi, and the cultivation of opium in Sichuan, Fujian, Yunnan, and Guizhou, which have been criticized by the people, the policy of complete prohibition should not be wavered. If the anti-opium authorities act inconsistently and recognize opium as a legally permitted business, it would not only violate the previously promulgated anti-opium law, but also violate the KMT's platform, international treaties, and the teachings of the late Premier.

Our Society is dedicated to promoting the wishes of the people and considers it our duty to oppose this disastrous policy, which endangers the country and harms the people. At the recent Fourth Plenary Session, Party and government officials reiterated the decision to strictly ban opium. If public sale is implemented, the reputation of the country and the livelihood of the people will be unimaginable. Our Society feels deeply threatened and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we respectfully submit this petition, urging the Central Government to instruct the National Anti-Opium Bureau to effectively ban opium and other drugs, to order the abolition of the special tax offices in Hunan and Hubei, as well as the public sale bureaus in Guangdong and Guangxi, and to strictly prohibit the promotion of opium public sale by instructing party branches at all levels throughout the country, in order to rectify public opinion and safeguard the Party's platform. At the same time, we request that anti-opium work be made a priority for all local party branches in order to attract public attention and increase the strength of opium prohibition. We urgently submit this petition and hope for your understanding.

Respectfully submitted to the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party.

Letter from Wu Liande to the Anti-Opium Society 90

Dr. Wu Liande sent a letter yesterday to the Chinese National Anti-Opium Society, stating:

I have learned that your Society included my name on the list of executive committee members without first obtaining my consent. I believe that everyone shares the same concern for anti-opium affairs, and this aligns with my own long-held aspirations. Therefore, I did not hold you responsible for your presumptuous action. However, since then, I have not received any notification from your Society regarding any internal or external affairs, and I only see my name listed on various documents. I believe that all the other esteemed gentlemen listed are prominent figures of our time, and the matters they are involved in are of concern to everyone.

Recently, I have been concerned about the spread of opium and narcotics, which not only harms China but is also spreading globally. I have also been asked by well-intentioned people at home and abroad to propose thorough measures for opium prohibition for everyone to discuss. Overwhelmed by grief, how could I refuse to contribute my efforts? Therefore, based on my decades of experience, I published an article titled "The Extremely Harmful Opium Problem," which is purely my personal opinion for the people of China to study and consider. It does not represent the position of any organization or group, nor is it intended to be submitted to the authorities. It is simply one opinion on a problem that everyone should study, with the aim of completely eliminating opium and ending the futile rhetoric that allows opium to flourish. I never expected that your Society would misunderstand me and falsely accuse me of advocating opium public sale.

I have long regarded opium, a harmful substance that has severely harmed our country, as the greatest shame and enemy of the Chinese nation. Therefore, I have devoted decades to studying the problem of opium prohibition. I cannot guarantee the correctness of my views, but I am certainly not engaging in empty rhetoric or hiding ulterior motives to seek advancement. To achieve factual results, one cannot simply stare straight ahead but must first calmly study all practical methods. Moreover, my article does not contain a single word about public sale. I do not know where your Society obtained the statement "Wu Liande openly advocates the implementation of opium public sale in the newspapers." I am afraid that this is based on misinformation.

Yesterday, I met Mr. Tang Shaochuan, whom your Society calls the Honorary Chairman. He said that he was initially invited to attend the temporary Standing Committee meeting on the 13th, but he declined. Then, the Secretary-General of your Society, Mr. Huang Jiaohui, and two or three others moved to his residence for a tea party. Mr. Huang made many unfair remarks, giving the impression of restricting my freedom of speech. Mr. Tang repeatedly corrected him, indicating his dissatisfaction with Mr. Huang's words and actions. Later, I saw in various newspapers that "Honorary Chairman Tang so-and-so" had discussed and decided on seven or eight proposals.

The purpose of your Society is anti-opium. I am grateful for the support of all sectors of society. However, how can someone as inexperienced as Mr. Huang turn good intentions into a constant blame? Alas, I have served the motherland for nearly thirty years and have spent just as long studying the opium problem. Due to other responsibilities, I have been unable to devote myself entirely to anti-opium efforts. Even basic measures, such as establishing opium addiction treatment hospitals to provide opium addicts with the opportunity to quit, have not yet been established. Powerful individuals continue to cultivate and sell opium, and we are powerless to stop them. Large sums of money are spent on anti-opium efforts, but opium continues to spread throughout the country. I ask myself, can I not feel ashamed? I have the heart to serve the country, but my temples have turned white. However, I dare not show weakness. However, everyone has their own ambitions, and I cannot force them to agree with me. If someone like the formidable Mr. Huang Jiaohui is going to be like this, how can I dare to associate with him again?

Therefore, I am writing to inform you that your Society is not allowed to use my name as an executive committee member from now on, in order to clarify the situation.

Sincerely,

Wu Liande

Various Industry Tax Regulations Committee Replies to Various Associations 92

Regarding the Business Tax Case

The Municipal Committee on Tax Regulations for Various Industries sent a letter yesterday to various trade associations, including the fur industry, cotton cloth industry, and seafood industry, stating:

We have received your letter and, after gathering and studying the results, we propose that the business tax rate should not exceed two per thousand, unless otherwise stipulated by the government to be below two per thousand. The wholesale portion should still be taxed at one-quarter of the rate, and the collection should be handled in a simple and straightforward manner in order to eliminate harassment. Zhuangke who do not engage in buying or selling activities should be exempt from business tax to avoid double taxation.

On February 7th, we sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting that it be forwarded for review and handling. On February 14th, we sent a telegram directly to the Ministry of Finance, requesting strict correction when amending the business tax in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. The full text of these letters is published in the local newspapers of February 7th and 15th, which we hope you have seen. If the above proposals can achieve their intended purpose, then the various points raised in your letter will be resolved easily.

This letter serves as a reply, and we hope that your association will continue to contribute its views so that we can gather and study them and submit them to the financial authorities for adoption.

Sincerely,

To the Trade Associations of the Fur Industry, Copper and Tin Industry, Silk Fabric Industry, Western Clothing Industry, Candle Industry, ____ Industry, Ham Industry, Firecracker Industry, Cosmetic Industry, Leather and Grass Goods Industry, Paint Industry, Liang Shaojiu Industry, Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry, Cotton Cloth Industry, Embroidery Industry, Seafood and Grocery Industry, Egg Industry, Fur Industry, and New Medicine Industry

News from the Transportation Sector 94

Trains, Buses, and Trams Operate as Usual: Today is the abolished Lunar New Year's Day, which has been ordered to be abolished by the government authorities. According to news from the transportation sector yesterday, trains on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo lines will operate as usual, and the timetable will remain the same. The public bus company and tram company, fearing that drivers and ticket sellers would be attached to the old customs and ask for leave under false pretenses, posted a notice yesterday stating that no leave would be granted for the abolished Lunar New Year's Day. Those who ask for leave for one day under false pretenses will have two days' wages deducted.

Huashang Third Route Tram Reduces Prices Yesterday: The Huashang Tram Company's third route circular tram, which operates around the city, has been convenient for citizens since its launch. At the same time, the French Tram Company's third route tram also operates on the Route to China of the French Concession from Xiaodongmen to Laoximen. However, the Huashang Tram Company's business on this route has been taken over by the French Tram Company. Yesterday (the 16th), due to the end of the abolished Lunar New Year, citizens traveled to and from shopping, and the trams were very crowded. Extra trips were added, operating from 6:00 AM to 1:00 AM, and the fares for these trams were reduced for one day. First-class tickets were priced the same as second-class tickets.

Huashang Public Bus Fourth Route Postponed: The Zhabei Huashang Public Bus Company previously planned to open a fourth bus route, starting from the Baoshan Road intersection to the area of Jungong Road and Xiangyin Road, directly to Shanghai University, passing through Chizhi University and Fudan University, to facilitate transportation for all sectors. Yesterday afternoon, the company received instructions from the Municipal Public Works Bureau to postpone the review.

Severe Cold in North China Hinders Shipping Again 95

Tianjin Freezes for the Second Time: The Baihe River in Tianjin was blocked by ice during the severe cold last month, trapping more than 20 ships bound for Tianjin from Shanghai and other ports. It took more than a week for them to break free. Recently, the Baihe River was gradually thawing, and Shanghai-bound Chinese ships were planning to resume service. However, news arrived that since the 14th, the cold in Tianjin and Dagukou had increased sharply, and the Baihe River had frozen for the second time, even more severely than before. Sixteen or seventeen ships in the harbor were unable to sail and were trapped by the ice. Recently, ships from Shanghai to Tianjin have been able to reach only 20 miles outside Tanggu before dropping anchor. Passengers and cargo are transferred to small boats for landing. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Beiyang service has been postponed again.

Qinhuangdao Also Closed: Qinhuangdao does not usually freeze, so the port is not closed. However, due to the severe cold this time, Qinhuangdao has also frozen, the port has been closed, and shipping routes have been blocked. The Kailan Mining Administration's coal, which is usually unloaded there, has also been blocked and cannot be shipped out. The Shanghai office received a telegram yesterday and announced that it has stopped selling coal. It must wait until the ice thaws before it can be transported to Shanghai for sale.

Shipping Industry Breaks with Lunar New Year Shutdown 96

This year, the national calendar is being strictly implemented, breaking with the tradition of shutting down during the Lunar New Year. The suspension of service by various commercial ships varies. The news obtained yesterday is recorded below:

Yangtze River Ships: British Taikoo Dockyard Yangtze River ships have suspended service since yesterday and will resume service on the 20th. The Japanese Gonghe Wheel will change to sail out tomorrow. The Japanese Qing Company will close for one day today and resume normal service tomorrow. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Sanbei Company, etc., will suspend service due to repairs or lack of cargo and will resume normal service starting next week.

Shanghai-Ningbo Ships: Ningbo ships like the New Beijing have already stopped sailing. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Ning Shao will not stop sailing. Yesterday, the New Ning Shao exported only 160 pieces of cargo from Ningbo, earning only 70 taels in freight, and there were very few passengers. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Sanbei service today will probably go to Ningbo empty.

Zhehai Ships: Most of the six Zhehai ships to Shantou have stopped sailing. Recently, they have been busy increasing the escort fleet and passenger tickets. The six companies have agreed to resume service on the 20th. The Tongyang Wheel will also stop service for one day today and resume service tomorrow.

Inland River Ships: The inland river ships on the Suzhou-Wuxi-Changzhou-Hangzhou-Huzhou routes stopped service early. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's small ships also planned to close for five days. After receiving an official letter from the Social Affairs Bureau, they were not allowed to suspend service without authorization. The six inland river ship companies reached a compromise at a meeting the day before. During this suspension period, the six companies will cooperate and operate one ship each day. Even if it is empty, the loss will be small, in order to comply with government orders and show that they are strictly implementing the national calendar.

Negotiations Regarding Damage from Paper Horse Racing 101

The holding of paper horse races by foreigners in the Chinese countryside was originally ordered to be prohibited by our government officials. Normal Service Today

Passenger fares will be three yuan per person in first class cabins, two yuan in room cabins, and the original price in third class cabins, five jiao per person, seven jiao and five fen per person in the Si Chuan Pavilion and Lattice Shop, and twelve yuan per person in the Da Cai Room. Round-trip tickets will be cancelled. Furthermore, the ships on this line usually suspend service for several days during the old Lunar New Year. Now, in order to comply with the national calendar, they will operate as usual during the abolished Lunar New Year.

The Labor Dispute at the China Can Manufacturing Factory Still Awaits Continued Mediation 106

The labor strike at the Japanese-owned China Metal Can Manufacturing Factory on Jixiang Road in Hongkou has lasted for a long time. The Social Affairs Bureau has dispatched personnel and convened mediation meetings several times, but to no avail due to the persistence of the management. Yesterday at 1:00 PM, the bureau continued to convene a mediation committee to conduct mediation. Representatives from the management, Konishi Chotaro and Koyama Shigeki, and representatives from the labor side, Xie Shixian and Guo Shuangdeng, attended. Wang Bing from the Social Affairs Bureau, Chen Timin from the Public Security Bureau, and Zhu Yakui from the Municipal Civil Training Committee served as the chairmen and members of the committee. Yu Zhiqin served as the recorder. After a long discussion, the labor and management sides reached an agreement on (1) worker Lin Kang being allowed to return to work, and wages for the strike period being paid from the date of the order; (2) the issue of the shutdown period for all workers being resolved. Later, the management representative suddenly proposed that, in order to increase production efficiency, the workers' wage requirements be changed to a contract system. The chairman, in accordance with Article 8 of the Implementing Regulations of the Labor Dispute Handling Law, stated that no new conditions were allowed to be raised before the case was resolved. However, due to the management representative's insistence, the chairman announced that the mediation would continue at 1:00 PM on the 18th.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Reports a Dispute in the Organization of the Woodworking and Painting Industries 107

No Mediation Possible

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday reported to the Social Affairs Bureau and the Civil Training Committee regarding an organizational dispute between the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry and the Painting Industry, stating that: "The report is in response to the case. On January 16th of this year, Order No. 5802 from the Social Affairs Bureau stated that, according to a report from the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry Association, the Painting Industry Association had sent people to woodworking shops to solicit membership, requesting correction and attaching the association's constitution and a solicitation for membership, etc. According to this, whether the claims made by each are true or not concerns an industrial dispute, and it is appropriate to examine and submit a report. You are hereby ordered to comply, promptly investigate and clarify, and report the situation impartially. Attached is the original report, the constitution, and the solicitation for membership. The association received these documents and, on January 30th, the Civil Training Committee also instructed the association to promptly dispatch personnel to investigate and mediate and report the situation. After receiving the instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau, the association immediately dispatched personnel to investigate. According to the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry Association, the 'paoli shui bang' who join the painting industry are distinct from Western-style woodworking shops in terms of workshops. The so-called internal woodworking dowry shops are painting workshops attached to Chinese-style woodworking shops. A woodworking shop must have a painting workshop attached, and its participation in a group should follow the guidance of the main body. When asked how many woodworking shops had joined, they claimed that there were 29 Western-style woodworking shops and a few Chinese-style woodworking shops. According to the Painting Industry Association, the association was initiated and built by sign painters, exterior painters of ships, and interior painters of wooden dowries. In the 23rd year of Guangxu, painters of automobiles and carriages joined after donating funds. In the 8th year of the Republic of China, painters of round objects joined. In the 10th year of the Republic of China, painters of small objects and other six groups joined, forming the association. In the 15th year of the Republic of China, the Shanghai County Chamber of Commerce convened representatives from the six groups, donated funds to purchase a base in southern Shanghai, and reported to the former Shanghai County, which issued a proclamation. Since being ordered to reorganize, the so-called Chinese and Western woodworking shops have all been included. When asked how many woodworking shops had joined, they claimed that almost all Chinese-style woodworking shops and fewer than ten Western-style woodworking shops had joined. Given the situations of the two industries as described above, the association convened representatives from both industries to come to the association on January 29th to listen to mediation. At that time, the painting industry, due to past historical relationships, insisted on merging the organizations. The Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry, however, refused to merge, citing the different main bodies and different natures. The association then proposed mediation opinions, stating that, in terms of business nature, the painting industry is a type of engineering that processes and manufactures goods sold. It cannot include the main body of its own industry. Therefore, Chinese and Western woodworking shops should join the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry Association. However, the painting industry has assets, and part of them were purchased with donations from the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry. Forcing them to leave the painting industry and join the woodworking industry would not benefit either side and would only cause disputes. Since only three Chinese-style woodworking shops have joined the Woodworking Industry Association, and fewer than ten Western-style woodworking shops have joined the Painting Industry Association, it would be better to directly rename the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry Association as the Western-style Woodworking Industry Association, transfer the three Chinese-style woodworking shops that have joined the association to the Painting Industry Association, and allow the paoli shui bang members and Western-style woodworking shops that have joined the Painting Industry Association to join the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry Association within a certain period. Otherwise, if, as the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry claims, every woodworking shop must have a painting workshop attached, then the painting part should join the Painting Industry Association, and the woodworking part should join the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry Association in order to resolve the issue. After discussion, neither industry adopted the mediation method, and the meeting adjourned without results. Later, the Civil Training Committee ordered the association to investigate, mediate, and report the case. The association then scheduled another mediation for February 10th. Unexpectedly, at that time, the Chinese and Western Woodworking Industry Association submitted a letter stating that, although they had been convened, there would be no good results, and refused to attend. Given the situation, the association believes that there is no possibility of further mediation. The association hereby submits a report on the handling of the case in accordance with the instructions to your bureau for review. Regarding the two mediation methods proposed by the association, whether they can be adopted for future reference in resolving this case awaits your decision."

Dr. Rowerden to Lecture on Air 108

Dr. Rowerden, a scientist of the Shanghai YMCA Scientific Lecture Department and a famous American scientist, lectures on scientific issues in various parts of our country every year. He uses self-made instruments to illustrate the basic principles of sound, light, force, electricity, and various physical sciences. Therefore, wherever he goes, people from all walks of life welcome him. The doctor has served the YMCA of China for twenty-eight years and will return to the United States this spring. He is scheduled to hold a special three-day lecture at the YMCA lecture hall on the 24th, 25th, and 26th of this month, inviting friends from all walks of life to attend as a farewell commemoration. The general topic of this lecture is "The Lubricity of Air," from the attraction of white molecules to the rotation and operation of celestial bodies, encompassing everything. There will also be ingenious instruments to assist, making it easy for listeners to understand. Listening to this speech is better than reading a science book.

The Seaport Quarantine Station Adds a Rat Testing Department 111

Hoping for Cooperation from Ship and Warehouse Owners

The National Seaport Quarantine Station, in order to prevent the spread of plague and other rodent-borne diseases, has recently added a rat testing department, hiring experts to specialize in testing domestic rats and other rodents in warehouses, barges, and small boats. If plague germs are found, they can be immediately disinfected to prevent the spread to the port and incoming and outgoing ships. It is hoped that the owners of warehouses, barges, and small boats will comply with the quarantine regulations and cooperate with the station.

The Hotel Industry Resolves on Measures to Suppress River Bandits on the Huangpu River 112

Submitting to the Two Bureaus for Adoption

River bandits on the Huangpu River have always been rampant. The Municipal Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus have jointly issued proclamations, strictly ordering their suppression. However, the river bandits are bold and reckless, paying lip service and acting in defiance. The Municipal Hotel Industry Association convened a joint meeting on the 5th with the hotel members who hire outer river receptionists, who are more closely related to this matter, and discussed the matter repeatedly and seriously, resolving on four fundamental measures: (1) Limit the registration of rowing boats and strictly investigate illegal activities; (2) Set fixed passenger fares and strictly prohibit extortion; (3) Detain the ringleaders and sign repentance pledges; (4) Plant signs at each wheel pier, stipulating the prices for porters to carry luggage, prohibiting collusion and fraud, and excessive solicitation of tips. They also submitted detailed measures, requesting the Municipal Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus to find ways to adopt and actively suppress them to reassure travelers. It is reported that the two bureaus have sent personnel to consult in order to adopt and implement them.

The China Child Welfare Association Benefits Blind and Deaf Orphans 115

A blind child, about six years old, abandoned by a woman surnamed Lu at No. 11 Xinlu Inn, North Railway Station, Kene Road, was sent to the Special District Court by the Shanghai Municipal Police. The French Concession Postpones Doctor Registration Inspection and Penalties 116

With the Help of Li Heng and Others

The Shanghai National Medicine Association previously found the doctor registration in the French Concession to be quite troublesome. They drafted opinions and sent a letter to the French Concession Health Department for adoption and amendment. Yesterday, representatives Liu Liheng, Ding Jiaohua, and Jiang Wenfang contacted the department and were received by General Manager Ai Jun. The representatives explained their intentions, and Ai Jun replied that the association's intentions were clear. Regarding the three points presented, the board of directors would discuss them and give a satisfactory reply. The representatives then requested that, as the regulations were just beginning to be implemented, the industry was not yet clear about them, and it seemed unfair to impose penalties hastily. In addition to requesting a prompt reply to the points presented by the association, the enforcement should not be enforced again within a reasonable period. Also, as the association is a formal legal entity in Shanghai, and all members are formal national doctors, if registration is required, could the association be entrusted to submit the documents? Ai Jun replied that if they were indeed members of the association and had proof, the association could submit the documents on their behalf. As for the enforcement period, it would be postponed until May 1st, and penalties would be waived before that date. The representatives then took their leave. It is also reported that the general manager has notified all police stations to investigate the suspension of penalties before May 1st.

Coal Gas Poisoning Relief and Prevention Methods 117

Social Affairs Bureau Receives Reply from Beiping Public Security Bureau

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau previously received a letter from Chen Taoan published in the Shishi News, explaining the methods for relieving and preventing coal gas poisoning, and stating that the Beiping Public Security Bureau had a good formula for relieving coal gas poisoning. The bureau then sent a letter to the Beiping Public Security Bureau to inquire. The bureau has now replied, stating that the method for relieving coal gas poisoning is currently under research and has not yet been tested. However, the common methods used in the north for relieving coal gas poisoning are: when someone feels the effects of coal gas early on, quickly carry the patient out of the courtyard and quickly irrigate them with hot cabbage soup or diluted grape juice. At the same time, artificial respiration can be used to restore consciousness. For Western medicine, ammonia water can be used to sniff under the patient's nose several times. As for prevention, before sleeping, the coal stove should be carried out of the courtyard, windows should be opened to circulate air, and the coal stove should not be placed in the bedroom with the windows tightly closed.

Four Robbers Leap Out of a Dark Alley 118

Zhu Dachang Stabbed

Four Robbers Flee After Robbery

Zhu Dachang, a bill collector for the China Textile Company, a native of Ningbo, 34 years old, residing at No. 29 Xujiahui Road, Shanghai West, collected 269 yuan in notes from the Jinfeng Silk Store on Ningbo Road yesterday afternoon at around 4:00 PM. He then walked out, turned into Henan Road, crossed the Pentang Lane Bridge, and went straight to the Huacheng Silk Store in Dean Lane, North Shanxi Road to collect debts. The store's accountant was not present, and a colleague told him to come back at around 6:00 PM. Zhu then said goodbye and left. When he reached Fenjia Yihang, at around 6:30 PM, he returned to the store. Unexpectedly, just as he reached the entrance of Dean Lane, four thugs emerged from the darkness. Two were wearing blue cloth shirts and pants, one was wearing a dark-colored cotton robe, and one was wearing a short coat, all wearing peaked caps. They rushed towards him, blocking his path. One of the robbers, wearing a black robe, spoke with a Hakka accent, saying to Zhu, "Be sensible, help us out." He then punched Zhu hard in the chest, and Zhu fell to the ground in pain. The robber then took out a sharp blade and stabbed Zhu in the foot, causing blood to flow freely. Another robber grabbed Zhu's throat with both hands, and the other two searched his pockets, finding a wallet filled with banknotes. They immediately told their companions, "Okay, okay," and fled into the side alleys without a trace. When Constable No. 151 arrived after hearing the alarm, the robbers were already far away. He could only send the injured man to Tongren Hospital for treatment. As for the amount of money robbed, it was not only 269 yuan, but also 20 yuan in Zhu's personal name, which was also completely robbed.

Mr. Shi Dezhi of Shi Dezhi's Divine Efficacy Salvation Water of the Shanghai Yaohua Pharmaceutical Factory 119

Mr. Shi Dezhi of the Shanghai Yaohua Pharmaceutical Factory invented Divine Efficacy Salvation Water, which has been sold for more than 30 years. Its efficacy is remarkable. The National Trademark Registration Bureau approved its registration. The Shanghai Municipal Council has granted it a special chemical test, proving that it is harmless. Foreign governments such as England, France, Japan, and their territories have also approved its distribution. In addition, Commander-in-Chief Chiang and Military and Political Minister He have awarded certificates. The Hong Kong Royal Hospital promotes it as a holy product among epidemic medicines. Therefore, overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia believe in it even more. Maritime officials, such as Commanders Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, and others, send gifts worth more than 100,000 yuan each year. Charitable organizations such as Jisheng Hui, Pushan Villa, and the Hunan Charity Association purchase huge amounts for distribution every summer and autumn to save the poor.

Huangpu River Bridge Project 120

Meng An Company Has Not Signed a Formal Contract

On the 10th of this month, various newspapers published the remarks of the initiator of the Huangpu River Bridge, in which it was mentioned that the bridge's construction project has been confirmed to be contracted by the Meng An Company, and that formal contracts have been signed. Female Student Suicide 121

Zhang Jingru's Thoughts are Distracted

Hu Fanruo Pays Attention to Detail

The Lover Gun Case is Strange

Zhang Jingru, a female student at Datong University at the South Railway Station, committed suicide with a sharp blade in the school dormitory at around 10:00 AM yesterday. The school discovered this and immediately sent her to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. Unfortunately, she died at around 11:00 AM due to her serious injuries. The details obtained are recorded below.

Entrance Process: Zhang Cishu, a native of Xuzhou, resides at the west end of Mao Pu Street in Pei County, Xuzhou. He has two sons and three daughters. The youngest daughter is Jingru, who is 19 years old. She is beautiful, quiet, and taciturn. Two years ago, because her brother Daoyuan was studying in the university department of Datong University in Shanghai, Jingru also came to Shanghai alone, applied to the school, and was admitted to the junior high school. She got along well with teachers and students. Time passed quickly, and a semester passed in the blink of an eye. Jingru packed her bags and returned home. For some reason, Jingru did not return to the school when the next semester started, and the teachers suspected that she had transferred to another school, so they did not pay attention to it. On February 1st of this year, the opening date of Datong University, Principal Cao Huijun suddenly received a letter by post. After opening it, he learned that it was sent by Zhang Jingru, stating that she wanted to re-enter the school, but did not know whether to take the exam again, so she came to inquire. At that time, Principal Cao replied that Jingru was a former student, and if she re-entered the first year of junior high school, she could be exempted from the exam. On the 5th, Jingru brought her luggage to the school. After paying the tuition fees as usual, the school handled it as a former student qualification, without requiring her to fill out a guarantee form. She was assigned to live in dormitory No. 19.

Claiming Illness and Seeking Medical Treatment: On the 6th of this month, all school students went to class, but Jingru stayed in the dormitory, not going out all day. She only started attending class the next morning, but the students did not see anything unusual. On the afternoon of the 9th, Jingru suddenly had a headache and wanted to ask for half a day off. Teacher Hu Fanruo allowed her to do so, and Jingru walked into the dormitory, got into bed, and rested. On the morning of the 10th, Jingru again asked Teacher Hu for another half-day off, so that she could go to a hospital outside the school to seek medical treatment. Hu thought that going out to seek medical treatment was a common occurrence and granted her leave. Jingru happily left the school and returned at around 11:00 AM, going straight to the dormitory. Her roommates asked how she was after the treatment. Jingru said that she felt a little better after the doctor gave her an injection and that she was about to take medicine. The students heard this and offered to pour her hot water, but Jingru firmly refused. Later, she took a cup of hot water herself, faced the glass window, and swallowed the medicine. However, the students did not know what kind of medicine she had taken. Jingru went to sleep after taking the medicine and did not attend class in the afternoon. In the evening, Hu felt strange and went to the dormitory to check on Jingru's condition. He saw that Jingru was extremely tired and her pulse was faint. Knowing that her illness had worsened, he urgently called Dr. Cai to come for a diagnosis, but he did not know the cause of her illness.

Sent to the Hospital: On the 11th, fearing that something dangerous would happen, he immediately sent Jingru to Shanghai Hospital for diagnosis, but still did not know what she was suffering from. Seeing that she was mentally exhausted, he gave her a strong heart injection. Her spirits only improved slightly in the evening. On the 12th, Hu, finding her illness strange, went to her dormitory to check for any abnormalities. After searching for a long time, he suddenly found an empty bottle of tranquilizer on the windowsill, and an empty box of tranquilizer pills outside the window. He realized that Jingru had committed suicide by taking poison, not by being ill. He immediately sent a letter to summon her family to Shanghai and rushed to Shanghai Hospital to report to the doctor, immediately finding a way to rescue her. In the evening, Jingru insisted on returning to school. The hospital, because the poison had been eliminated, said she was safe and allowed her to return to school. Jingru had returned to school.

Zhou Ma Takes Care: Hu, fearing that another accident would happen, hired a maid, Zhou Ma, to serve her and told her to pay attention to monitor everything. On the 13th, Hu went to ask her why she committed suicide. Jingru said that one of her classmates was the most vicious and wanted to take revenge. I was wronged by him. This is caused by the evil society. You are my dear teacher, please keep it a secret and do not announce my poisoning to others. Hu readily agreed. On the 14th, Hu went to visit her again. Jingru took 32 yuan and entrusted Hu to deposit it in the school. She also wrote a letter and entrusted him to mail it on her behalf. The gist of the letter was that her illness had recovered and asked her parents not to come to Shanghai, and that she planned to transfer to another school again. Hu, fearing another accident, collected the original letter. On the 15th (the day before yesterday), at around 6:00 AM, Jingru suddenly walked into Hu's bedroom, asking for leave to go out for medical treatment. Hu told her to wait, but she left angrily. Before long, Jingru learned that the original letter had not been mailed, and sent Zhou Ma to ask for it back.

Slitting Her Throat and Dying: At around 10:00 AM yesterday, Zhou Ma suddenly rushed to tell Hu that something bad had happened. Hu suspected that Jingru had fallen ill, and rushed into the dormitory for a close look. He opened the bed curtains and saw that Jingru was still holding a small foreign blade in her hand, covered in blood. Blood was gurgling from her neck, and the bed curtains were stained with blood. He realized that she had slit her throat and was shocked. He quickly prepared a car to send her to Shanghai Hospital, but she died at around 11:00 AM. The case was reported to the First Section of the First District, and Qin Defang, the local captain of the 23rd lane, was instructed to report to the Shanghai District Court for an autopsy. Her body has been returned to the school by the school.

Is it Zhang Biyue?: It was also found that the female student Zhang Jingru was the lover of Zhang Biyue, who caused a national sensation two years ago when she shot and killed her sister. Unexpectedly, she changed her name and came to Shanghai to study, enrolling in Datong University. There may be an unspeakable inside story in this sudden suicide.

A Pitiable Story of Wu Daosheng’s Tragic Suicide 122

Failed to Find Work After Coming from Beiping

Incited by Others, Divorced His Wife

Faced Hardship After Remarrying

Overwhelmed with Emotions, Committed Suicide by Poison

Wu Daosheng, from Beiping, was thirty-seven years old. He used to work in the Accounting Section of the State Council during the Beiyang Government era. He also served as the director of a tobacco and alcohol monopoly bureau near Zhangjiakou. Seven years ago, he married his cousin Yao Baoru (currently twenty-five years old and a primary school graduate). After the Nationalist government moved south, Wu became unemployed, becoming a "disaster official." His household consisted only of him and his wife.

Finding Life Unbearable in the North, in the seventeenth year [of the Republic], he managed to scrape together seven thousand yuan and came to Shanghai with his wife's younger sister to seek employment. After arriving in Shanghai, they rented a room downstairs at No. 105 Xiexing Lane, Baoxing Road, Zhabei, at the house of Shen Mingsan (formerly employed at the Guangdong Mint). He sought employment from former Shanghai Mayor Zhang Ding, but without success. In Shanghai, he lent out the money he had brought with him and lived off the interest. His wife's younger sister recognized Mr. and Mrs. Shen as her adoptive parents. Unexpectedly, the Shens incited discord between Wu and his wife, leading to quarrels and disharmony.

Wu's wife's younger sister died of illness, and Wu's money, apart from a thousand or so gold yuan that he had lent out with receipts, was mostly borrowed and exhausted by others. At this point, the relationship between Wu and his wife deteriorated further. In the seventh month of the lunar calendar last year, they divorced through mediation by the Shens and others. Yao, because her younger sister had died,

Felt Alone and Abandoned in Shanghai, and without relatives, conceived the idea of suicide. She took poison in a hotel, but fortunately, the tea boy discovered her and sent her to Guangren Hospital, where she was saved. The hospital, seeing her pitiable situation, recommended her to work as a nanny at Datong Kindergarten at the intersection of Gordon Road and Wuding Road. In August, Wu married

A Muslim woman named Yang from Qingjiang, Yang Xiuhua (eighteen years old this year), and rented a room at No. 1126 and a half Taide Lane, Xinzha Road. Yang's mother and brother lived with them, depending on Wu for support. A month ago, Wu felt that his funds were depleted and life was difficult. Although he had divorced Yao Baoru, he still maintained contact with her as a relative and sought her help in finding employment. He expressed regret for having listened to

Other's Incitement to Divorce and showed signs of being tired of the world and wanting to kill himself. Yao comforted him and promised to help him find a job. Later, Wu found that the rent was too high and he could not afford it. He discussed with Yao, seeking help to sell his bedding and furniture to move to a smaller place and reduce expenses. Yao again helped him by mortgaging the items for sixty yuan, which he gave to Wu, telling him that he could redeem them later when he found a job. After getting the money, Wu moved to the upper floor of Yushengxiang Chicken and Duck Shop on Chi Bang Bridge, Xinzha Road. Before long, Wu again complained that the

House was too small and unsuitable, and asked Yao to help him find a solution. She promised to help him find a place for Wu to stay temporarily in a church. Wu also entrusted Yao with the receipts for the loans he had made, asking her to find a lawyer to recover the debts. When Wu's current wife Yang Hua and her mother and brother found out about this, they suspected that Yao had bad intentions and wanted to entice Wu to live with her, so they kept Wu under surveillance at home and prevented him from going out. As a result, Wu felt economically strapped and was prevented from having freedom and had difficulty finding employment. Overwhelmed with emotions,

He Conceived the Idea of Suicide. At 4:00 PM on the thirteenth of this month, he pretended to go out to collect debts to prepare for the New Year, telling his wife and mother-in-law that he was going out. He bought poison and went to the Aiduya Road No. 245 Hotel in the French Concession, where he registered under the name Zhao Guangyu from Shandong. After booking a room, he wrote two letters. One letter detailed how he, his wife, and her younger sister came to Shanghai seeking employment without success, how his wife and he were incited to divorce by the Shens, and how his money was borrowed and cheated away. He blamed himself for being foolish and

Expressed Weariness of the World and Suicidal Thoughts. The other letter was addressed to his divorced wife Yao, expressing his apologies and asking her to consider their family ties, to arrange for the collection of his body, and to bring it back to his hometown in the future. After writing the letters, he took the poison and committed suicide. It was not until 2:00 PM the next day that the tea boy discovered him. He was already dead. The police were notified and the body was taken to the forensic examination office of the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall to await examination. The details have been briefly reported on the fifteenth. Subsequently, the detective, according to the address on the letter, notified the family members Yao Binru and Yang Xiuhua to come to the station. Yesterday, Zhu, the presiding judge of the criminal court of the French Concession, came to the office to examine the body and confirmed that the deceased had indeed

Died by Poisoning Himself While Alive. The detective also submitted the deceased's will as evidence. Yao stated that she was willing to claim the body for burial. Judge Zhu then ordered Yao Binru to prepare a coffin for burial. Yao then managed to provide clothing and a coffin, and hastily arranged for the burial and temporarily placed the coffin in the cemetery.

Factory Owner Seduces Neighbor's Daughter 123

Engages in Conduct of Beginning with Affection and Abandoning

Uncaring for a Newborn

Shen Meimei Laments Her Unfortunate Fate

Shen's Mother Appeals to the Law

Zhong Xiaoqi, the fifth son of Mr. Zhong, a Cantonese owner of a sock factory in Weishui Lane, Zhejiang Road, is a frivolous young man who enjoys chasing after women. His neighbor, a widow named Shen Zhu (also known as Shen Li), from Suzhou, has a daughter named Meimei, who is twenty-nine years old and still unmarried.

Xiaoqi Admired Her Beautiful Appearance and used various tricks to seduce her. The girl, who was of marriageable age and had once been a registered entertainer, not only did not reject his advances but welcomed them. Thus, they formed an inseparable bond, meeting frequently in hotels, while the girl's mother remained unaware. Before long,

The Girl Conceived a Child. Xiaoqi then disappeared without a trace and stopped seeing the girl. The girl lamented her unfortunate fate and being abandoned midway. The girl's mother also noticed that her abdomen was gradually swelling and questioned her severely. The girl could no longer hide the truth and confessed everything. The mother hated Xiaoqi for ruining her daughter's chastity and then abandoning her. After she gave birth in a hospital last month, she hired lawyer Shen Xingxia to sue Zhong Xiaoqi in the Special District Local Court,

Charging Zhong with Seduction. The complaint stated that the defendant had seduced a girl under the age of twenty and abandoned the child she bore. According to the law, he should be sentenced to imprisonment for one to seven years and fined up to one thousand yuan. Furthermore, those who abandon persons who are unable to help themselves, who are required to be supported, raised, and protected by law or contract, shall be sentenced to imprisonment for six months to five years. In this case, the second plaintiff,

Shen Meimei, is Eighteen Years Old, and her intelligence is not fully developed. She was seduced by the defendant and ran away from her mother. Initially, there were sweet words and letters back and forth, but then he abandoned the old for the new, making excuses to avoid her and disappearing without a trace. Finally, he abandoned the child she bore, which constitutes the criminal acts mentioned above. The plaintiff requests that the defendant be summoned to court and punished, and also requests a judgment for current support and

Expenses for Childbirth, a portion of which amounts to one thousand yuan. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao opened the fifth criminal court for trial. First, the plaintiff's lawyer, Shen Xingxia, stated that Shen Meimei was ill after childbirth and could not attend court. He requested a seven-day postponement until she recovered and could testify. The court then summoned the defendant, who stated that he was from Guangdong and was twenty-two years old. When asked if Shen Meimei was his wife or concubine, Zhong replied that she was neither his wife nor his concubine. "Did you and Shen have a child?" Zhong answered, "The child is not mine. I am a neighbor,

Her family Runs a Club, and I often go there to play mahjong. I sometimes stay overnight at her house." Lawyer Shen then stated that Meimei's admission to the hospital for childbirth was done under the name of the Guangdong Sock Factory. The defendant denied this upon hearing this. Lawyer Shen then asked the defendant if he had opened a hotel room with Meimei. He replied, "Yes, I did. On September 23rd of last year, I returned to Shanghai from Hangzhou and stayed at the Pingqiao Hotel. I met Meimei on the way, and that's how we met.

That Night She Came to My Place, gave me ten yuan and asked me to buy her a watch. We went to the hotel together and slept in the same bed." Lawyer Shen then asked him if he had written any letters to Meimei. He answered, "Yes, I did. The letter generally said, 'You already have a handsome friend, and I can't afford to provide you with money now because my monthly salary is limited.'" Shen then requested a postponement and asked the defendant to post bail because his father had denied having such a son when the summons was first delivered to the defendant's store. Judge Xiao then granted the request, ordered the defendant to provide a surety who could be summoned at any time, and rescheduled the hearing for 2:00 PM on the 25th of this month.

A Young Woman's Suicide Attempt in the River 124

She Refuses to Explain the Reason

But Her Life is Not in Danger

Yesterday afternoon, around 5:30 PM, a woman with bobbed hair, wearing a green wool serge cheongsam with a vest and black velvet cotton shoes, was seen pacing back and forth along the Bund outside the Sima Road. A Chinese constable No. 1742, noticing her suspicious behavior, approached her and asked her what she was doing there and who she was waiting for. The woman did not answer. The constable, seeing that she was a young woman, did not press the matter and proceeded towards the Customs House. The woman, seeing that the constable had gone north, went to the riverside at 6:15 PM and jumped into the river to end her life and join the water deities. At that moment, a cargo barge nearby saw a woman jumping into the river to commit suicide and bravely rescued her. Fortunately, she had not been in the water for

Long and had swallowed little water, so she was still able to speak. However, she was shivering from the cold because her clothes were wet. By this time, the constable had returned from the Customs House and took the woman back to the main station on Sima Road. After questioning by detectives, she only stated that her surname was Chen, her given name was A'nan, she was twenty-six years old, a local, and lived at No. 6 Zhenyun Lane, Zhujia Bridge, but she refused to reveal why she had attempted suicide. The police then dispatched constable No. 1742 to take her to Renji Hospital and sent investigators to inquire about her family and the reason for her suicide. According to the staff at Renji Hospital, she was staying in room 55 on the fifth floor and was not in any danger.

Jiliang Institute Benefits Helpless Women 128

Dissolves Ru Yi's Engagement

Also Breaks Ties with Her Adoptive Mother

Zhou Yunlong from Tingzhou, who resides at No. 973 Yongkang Lane, Shanban Bridge, Maigen Road, is a fortune teller. In April of the year before last, he engaged his son to Ru Yi, the daughter of Ge Qin, a Zhili woman who lives next door. The girl was only thirteen years old and was raised as a child bride. Last autumn, the girl was abducted. The police arrested the abductor, surnamed Xu, and punished him. Because Ru Yi suffered abuse from her parents-in-law and did not want to return to Zhou's family, the Special District Local Court sent her to the Jiliang Institute for care. At the time of the incident, the girl's mother had returned to Tianjin and was unaware of the matter. She returned to Shanghai a few days ago and was informed of the incident by the matchmaker Zhu Shengcai. She went to Zhou's family to make accusations and sued Zhou for abusing her daughter. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ge of the Special Court opened the trial and summoned Ru Yi to testify. According to Ge Qin, Ru Yi was adopted by her when she was eight months old. She engaged her to Zhou's son through Zhu as a matchmaker two years ago for a bride price of thirty yuan. She was raised as a child bride. Later, the husband died, and the coffin was transported back to his hometown. Therefore, she did not know about Ru Yi's abduction at first. She is now requesting that the defendant return her daughter and the bride price. Zhou Yunlong stated in his defense that Ru Yi was engaged to my son with the consent of the plaintiff and his wife. After the abduction case was solved, Ru Yi did not want to return home and was sent to the Jiliang Institute temporarily. I did not abuse her. There is no reason for her lawsuit. If she insists on taking her away, she must return my bride price and other expenses of one hundred and thirty yuan. The matchmaker Zhu Shengcai also testified that the bride price was indeed one hundred and thirty yuan. Ru Yi testified that she is now fifteen years old, the plaintiff is my adoptive mother, and I now want to live permanently in the Jiliang Institute. I do not want to go to either my mother's house or my husband's house. A female director of the Jiliang Institute also came to court and presented her proposed compromise. The one hundred and thirty yuan requested by the plaintiff could be paid by the institute on her behalf, but Ru Yi must live there and her future marriage would also be decided by the institute. In this way, all three parties would benefit. Judge Ge then sought the opinions of the three parties regarding the opinions expressed by the director of the institute, and they all agreed. The judge ordered the director of the institute to pay one hundred and thirty yuan to the case, one hundred yuan to the defendants Zhou Yunlong and his wife, and thirty yuan to the plaintiff. He also ordered Zhou to submit Ru Yi's birth date, and Ge Qin was also ordered to submit the gift list she received. The marriage relationship was dissolved, and Ru Yi returned to the Jiliang Institute with the female director to await marriage when she grew older.
