World Tidbits 134

·Hai·Ke·

In British and American metropolises, several large laundries have as many as seventeen processes for washing collars.

The British ship "Faraday," famous for laying submarine cables, laid 50,000 miles of submarine cables in 48 years. It has now been retired.

The rickshaw was first invented in Japan. Therefore, it is commonly called the "Eastern Car." According to a survey conducted in January 1923, there were 300,000 rickshaws in Japan before 1922, circulating in the market. In recent years, the number has gradually decreased, and there are now fewer than 100,000.

A new type of thermometer has been invented in England. It is slightly larger than a man's watch. Inside, there is a special strip that changes with the weather. In cold weather, it can drop to ten degrees below freezing. In hot weather, it can rise to one hundred and thirty degrees.

The most famous opera in England, "The Beggar's Opera," has been performed 998 times. The actors in it were all the original cast. They were so familiar with the lines that they never made a mistake. Unexpectedly, during the 999th performance, one of the actors suddenly forgot his lines. Everyone thought it was strange.

The aviation industry in Europe is developing rapidly. Recently, someone manufactured a small plane that can fly 40 miles per hour. It has seating for one pilot and one passenger. The cost is only 150 British pounds per plane.

Anecdotes of Sun Baoqi 135

Ma Yili

Mr. Sun Baoqi, whose courtesy name was Muhanj, late in life using the sobriquet Meng Jin Old Man, was from the prestigious Wu Ling family. He held many important positions and served as an envoy to foreign countries. He was in politics for fifty years and was renowned for thirty years. After the party-state was stabilized, he retired to the south and settled in Shanghai. He had many children and was in dire straits. Mr. Sun was charitable and generous throughout his life and was not skilled in economics, so he served for many years but remained penniless. He died of illness in Shanghai last month. When the news came, everyone who knew him and who did not sighed and lamented. I have been favored by him and have no way to repay him. Writing this, I cannot help but feel grateful and ashamed. I will recount several anecdotes to encourage the world and show a small part of Mr. Sun's virtues.

During the Jiazi Qi-Lu War, Mr. Sun pleaded for his hometown, running around tirelessly. When he learned that the front line had actually opened fire, he sighed incessantly. When Lu Zijia invited him to a banquet at the governor's office, Mr. Sun tore up the invitation and went to the lake. The next morning, he left Hangzhou with the refugees, without anyone knowing.

The following year, Sun Xinyuan entered Zhejiang. Xia Chao, who was once his subordinate, was in charge of the provincial government. Xia expanded the police force, which was resented by Sun's troops, gradually creating an undercurrent. Both sides were on alert, and the situation was tense. Wang Zhuqi, Jin Baishun, and others tried to mediate without success. Finally, they pushed Mr. Sun forward. It was deep winter, late at night, and he was still bowing and apologizing in the military headquarters. He was able to not forget the safety of his hometown. He was truly admirable.

Mr. Sun upheld the ancient ways and was extremely filial. His younger brother Zhongyu was also the same. Zhongyu, whose given name was Baoxuan, once served as the superintendent of the Ningbo Customs. Every spring and autumn, they would return to their hometown together to visit relatives and sweep the tombs. They would always stay at the ancestral shrine of his late father-in-law, Zhang Qinguo. The shrine had beautiful scenery and was elegant and clean, making it a good place to stay. When the brothers had no social engagements, they would go to the lake. One moonlit night, they planned to row to Three Pools Mirroring the Moon, but there were no boatmen. I and my late brother Wenbin happened to be nearby and volunteered to row. Mr. Sun and his brother also rolled up their sleeves and helped, pushing through the wind and waves. The past is still vivid in my mind. Thinking of the past and comparing it to the present, I cannot help but feel sad.

When the prominent member of the Min Party, Mr. Jiang Guanyun, died in Shanghai, Mr. Sun supported himself with a cane and went to the funeral, wailing for a distance. Before the tears had dried, the news of another death arrived. His sixth sister, Madam Zhang, passed away from illness. He rushed there at night and wept over the coffin. Within three days, his old tears flowed frequently, and his eyes were almost dry. His deep feelings for his old friend were beyond what ordinary people could reach. When the party army set out, Mr. Sun retired to the south. Many important figures in the party-state praised him. Some asked him what he thought of Sun Yat-sen's doctrine. He would raise his thumb and say, "Good." He also said that he was very friendly with Sun Yat-sen. He especially praised Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek. He often cared about national affairs. Zhang Jingjiang, the governor of Zhejiang Province, hired him as a senior advisor. He made contributions from time to time. Therefore, Mr. Sun also made small contributions to the party-state.

Snow 136

Autumn Water

These past few days, Shanghai has had continuous heavy snow. It is truly beautiful to see. There is a saying: "Winter snow protects the five grains, spring snow protects the people." Now that we have both winter and spring snow, it is not only beautiful but also gratifying.

However, snow is currently more harmful than beneficial. Especially in transportation, snow is considered the number one enemy. What are the four major enemies? One is snow, two is fog, three is hail, and four is water. Fog can obscure the path, hail can damage vehicles, and water can flood the tracks. All of these are major enemies of transportation. In addition to obscuring the path, damaging vehicles, and flooding the tracks, snow can also crush power lines. You can imagine how harmful snow can be.

Snow is even more troublesome for trains. I still remember in 1866, there was heavy snow in several places in Northumberland, England. The snow was five or six feet high. The trains were almost completely buried in the snow. They could not move, and the passengers could not get out. Transportation personnel tried to remove the snow to rescue the passengers. However, some people waited for four days before the snow melted and they could leave the train. It was truly terrifying.

Therefore, railway bureaus in Europe and the United States must have specially made snowplows. Snowplows are made of steel or wood and weigh at least 26 tons. They have three pairs of wheels and are powered by a machine. There are also iron plates and brushes next to the wheels. In the snow or after the snow, they drive along the railway tracks, pushing the snow to the left and right and cleaning the tracks. The car has a stove for heating and a kitchen for making food. It can accommodate dozens of people. Because it takes one or two days of continuous work to clear the snow along the way after a snowfall.

Norfolk, England, had an unprecedented heavy snowfall in 1881. The trains there could not run, and the snowplows were difficult to operate. Because the snow was too heavy and the weather was too cold, the snowplow's engine was small and there was nothing that could be done. Finally, they borrowed eight train locomotives and pushed them behind the snowplow to generate heat and move forward. It was an interesting story in the snow.

Thirteen as a Lucky Number 137

Affairs · Politics

Zheng Baozhao and Thirteen

Mr. Zheng Yangsheng (Baozhao), the chief of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau, is a prominent railway expert in our country, known for his competence and diligence in handling affairs. I once chatted with him, and he mentioned that the number thirteen is often considered unlucky by Westerners. However, for him, it has a special connection. He recalled that after joining the International Savings Society for several years, he had never won any prizes, and he had long given up hope. Unexpectedly, one day, the society suddenly sent him several hundred yuan, saying it was prize money. He was surprised and delighted, and upon checking the calendar on his desk, he saw it was the 13th. Truly a coincidence.

Acknowledgments and Introduction: The Medical Review, edited by Mr. Chu Minyi, has been published for two years. Its purpose is to promote medical knowledge and discuss health facilities, and its value is unparalleled. We received a complimentary copy two weeks ago. Introduction to a Famous Epigrapher: Huang Junhanhou of Yangzhou is a renowned modern epigrapher, especially skilled in carving fans. He excels in all styles of calligraphy, including regular, cursive, seal, and official scripts, and his imitations are flawless. The fan bones he carves are no more than a foot long and only a few points wide. Some are engraved with the complete "Former and Latter Red Cliff Odes" or the "Former and Latter Memorials to the Throne," while others contain the entire "Sacred Teachings Preface" or the complete "Orchid Pavilion Preface" and thirteen postscripts. His imitations are so lifelike that the spirit and charm are not lost. The style is elegant and refined, with details as fine as mosquito legs, requiring a magnifying glass for those with slightly impaired vision to appreciate them fully. Major fan shops in Shanghai all carry Hanhou's works, and his fees are not excessive. You can write to Mr. Huang at Dazhuang in Duozijie, Yangzhou, for inquiries. I hereby introduce him to fellow enthusiasts.

Book Reviews

Qingping Monthly, Inaugural Issue 140

Tang Bin

The literary scene in Hangzhou has been unusually flourishing recently. Small-scale literary groups organized by young people who love literature have generally published regular periodicals, and their content is dedicated to promoting nationalistic literature. This is a good phenomenon in the literary world of inland China, undoubtedly influenced by the nationalistic literary movement in Shanghai. We must understand that modern Chinese literature lacks a correct central ideology, which has made the entire literary scene dark and chaotic. The confusion of thought is indescribable, and nothing is more detrimental to the bright future of young people than the Proletarian literature that was once popular. If we want to eliminate these corrupt and degenerate ideas, we can only promote a kind of literature with a clear ideology that young people need. In this way, incorrect ideas will be washed away invisibly.

The nationalistic literary movement has become the main trend in the Chinese literary world because it has a definite central ideology, and this is what the youth most need at present. We have seen that since the nationalistic literary movement was launched in Shanghai, there have been many periodicals and newspapers in various places that have responded to it. The "Qingping Monthly," which was discovered in the literary world of Hangzhou, is one of the most powerful of them.

The content of this inaugural issue is quite rich, such as Ding Leihong's "Play Wildly," Zheng Bo's "National Literature and Life," Youwei's "Heart Song," Xiaofeng's "Decent Gentleman," Gongzhu's "How Can You Lingeringly Cherish," Weiming's "For the Sake of Dishonesty," and Paixia's "Our World," etc., are all noteworthy works, at least in terms of ideological awareness.

In "Our Beginning," it is played wildly like this: "We have seized the era, this era occupies a very important part of the rhythm of our lives, but, friends, you must remember that this is easy to pass, and it will also disappear like the dark years of the past, in the invisible surroundings, in the ethereal fantasy, it disappears lightly, therefore, we need to have a deep understanding of life here, and then record it so ordinary, this understanding is very broad, it is a small model of our life, it is the radio of our shouts, ... we must record, record these ordinary stories, and at the same time, show the beautiful colors of the inner heart, as a memorial to the survival of our souls, because of this very small meaning, Qingping's buds are beginning to unfold today, along with us, we accept the inspiration of the new God of Destiny, relying on the bright and delicate flowers, to complete everything, friends who sympathize with us, please stand on the same front as us, pluck the heartstrings, and play wildly with all your might, take advantage of youth to take on this mission,"

After the wild playing that aroused our emotions, there is a powerful treatise 丨 National Literature and Life, although the content is somewhat simple, but the points discussed are very correct.

At the same time, the author also has a commentary on the Chinese literary world, which is also very true, as he said, "We see what kind of phenomenon is presented in the Chinese new literary world, since the vigorous new literature movement more than ten years ago, there have been many lively emotions and works with realization as the theme, but now the new literature does not seem to be progressing by leaps and bounds, and the spirit is unusually depressed," this is of course, its biggest shortcoming is still the lack of a correct central ideology, which makes Chinese new literature unable to develop, if we want to save the crisis in the Chinese literary world, that is, to make the new literature have some expression, then, we must promote national literature, the author also thought of this point, so in the end he ended like this, "Now it is the twentieth century, we should shoulder the mission of the literature required by this era, 丨 national literature 丨," if these young people work hard like this, they will definitely be able to get great results, but now there are already considerable achievements emerging before our eyes,

The two novels, "Decent Gentleman" and "For the Sake of Dishonesty," are both worth reading because their views are very correct, in fact, we can also regard them as ideal texts, in terms of poetry, especially some precious works, with rich emotions, upward consciousness, beautiful words, and encouraging maxims, because of the length of the article, I will not quote them one by one here,

In the literary world of Hangzhou, it is indeed a gratifying phenomenon to be able to give us such a powerful publication that promotes national literature, and, they have such a vigorous vitality in the embryonic stage, and the development in the future is of course unlimited, I sincerely make a careful recommendation here, which is a very meaningful thing, finally, I hope that the "Qingping" colleagues will work hard, and I hope that the literary world in Shanghai will pay attention to them,

Youth Garden

Returning from the Hospital 141

Anna

One Snowy Afternoon

All the way on the tram, the granular snowflakes, with the assistance of the north wind, were flying particularly lively in the air. Although I was wearing a coat and hat, I couldn't resist their attack. The more anxious I felt, the slower the tram seemed to be. My face felt like it was being pricked by thousands of needles.

The dark sky seemed even more drowsy. The street lights gradually increased. I thought of my family longing for me, especially my mother's distant thoughts. She would brave the wind and snow and stand in front of the door at this dusk, stretching her neck and waiting for her children who had gone out to study to return home. She was looking forward to it like a year, and the wrinkles between her eyebrows were gradually increasing. Great maternal love would make the weary traveler feel refreshed, and make people full of worries smile, and warm my frozen body...

Ah, great maternal love!

Thinking like this, smiling, I seemed to be standing in front of my mother, seeing her kind face and her gentle comfort, forgetting that I was still standing on this snowy ground, with a bag in my hand containing the heart, lungs, and liver of a fetus just dissected in the hospital.

This fetus was unfortunately a transverse presentation and died in the womb after a long period of time. He also suffered from inherited syphilis, as indicated by the enlargement of the liver. He was very good-looking, like a sleeping baby, with cheeks as red and lovely as duckweed. I didn't believe that he was a person who had left the world, a soulless person. Alas, I don't know why, I felt twelve points of pity and sympathy for this lovely and innocent fetus.

...

The dissection began, and the shining knife was on his abdomen.
